5.  is_checked() â†’ [bool][py3_bool] 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_Command_is_checked_}

    Return whether a checkbox should be shown next to the menu item. Command arguments are passed as keyword arguments. The .sublime-menu file must have the `"checkbox"` key set to `true` for this to be used.

6.  description() â†’ [str][py3_str] | [None][py3_None] 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_Command_description_}

    Return a description of the command with the given arguments. Command arguments are passed as keyword arguments. Used in the menu, if no caption is provided. Return `None` to get the default description.

7.  want_event() â†’ [bool][py3_bool] 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_Command_want_event_}

    Return whether to receive an [`Event`][Event] argument when the command is triggered by a mouse action. The event information allows commands to determine which portion of the view was clicked on. The default implementation returns `False`.

    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_EventListener_on_hover_}

    Called when the userâ€™s mouse hovers over the view for a short period.

    Parameters:

    `view`

    The view

    `point`

    `hover_zone`

    Which element in Sublime Text the mouse has hovered over.

34.  on_query_context(_view: [View][View]_, _key: [str][py3_str]_, _operator: [QueryOperator][QueryOperator]_, _operand: [str][py3_str]_, _match_all: [bool][py3_bool]_) â†’ [bool][py3_bool] | [None][py3_None] 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_EventListener_on_query_context_}

    Called when determining to trigger a key binding with the given context key. If the plugin knows how to respond to the context, it should return either True of False. If the context is unknown, it should return None.

    Parameters:

    `key`

    The context key to query. This generally refers to specific state held by a plugin.

    `operator`

    The operator to check against the operand; whether to check equality, inequality, etc.

    `operand`

    The value against which to check using the `operator`.

    `match_all`

    This should be used if the context relates to the selections: does every selection have to match(`match_all == True`), or is at least one matching enough (`match_all == False`)?

    Returns:

    `True` or `False` if the plugin handles this context key and it either does or doesnâ€™t match. If the context is unknown return `None`.

35.  on_query_completions(_view: [View][View]_, _prefix: [str][py3_str]_, _locations: List[[Point][Point]]_) â†’ [None][py3_None] | List[[CompletionValue][CompletionValue]] | Tuple[List[[CompletionValue][CompletionValue]], [AutoCompleteFlags][AutoCompleteFlags]] | [CompletionList][CompletionList] 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_EventListener_on_query_completions_}

    Called whenever completions are to be presented to the user.

    Parameters:

    `prefix`

    The text already typed by the user.

    `locations`

    The list of points being completed. Since this method is called for all completions no matter the syntax, `self.view.match_selector(point, relevant_scope)` should be called to determine if the point is relevant.

    Returns:

    A list of completions in one of the valid formats or `None` if no completions are provided.

26.  on_query_context(_key: [str][py3_str]_, _operator: [QueryOperator][QueryOperator]_, _operand: [str][py3_str]_, _match_all: [bool][py3_bool]_) â†’ [bool][py3_bool] | [None][py3_None]

27.  on_query_completions(_prefix: [str][py3_str]_, _locations: List[[Point][Point]]_) â†’ [None][py3_None] | List[[CompletionValue][CompletionValue]] | Tuple[List[[CompletionValue][CompletionValue]], [AutoCompleteFlags][AutoCompleteFlags]] | [CompletionList][CompletionList] 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_ViewEventListener_on_query_completions_}

    A list of completions in one of the valid formats or `None` if no completions are provided.

28.  on_text_command(_command_name: [str][py3_str]_, _args: [CommandArgs][CommandArgs]_) â†’ Tuple[[str][py3_str], [CommandArgs][CommandArgs]]  3155
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_ViewEventListener_on_text_command_}

    Called when a text command is issued. The listener may return a \`\` (command, arguments)\`\` tuple to rewrite the command, or `None` to run the command unmodified.

29.  on_post_text_command(_command_name: [str][py3_str]_, _args: [CommandArgs][CommandArgs]_) 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_ViewEventListener_on_post_text_command_}

    Called after a text command has been executed.

30.  _classmethod_ is_applicable(_settings: [Settings][Settings]_) â†’ [bool][py3_bool] 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_ViewEventListener_is_applicable_}

    Returns:

    Whether this listener should apply to a view with the given [`Settings`][Settings].

31.  _classmethod_ applies_to_primary_view_only() â†’ [bool][py3_bool] 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_ViewEventListener_applies_to_primary_view_only_}

    Returns:

    Whether this listener should apply only to the primary view for a file or all of its clones as well.

[ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_TextChangeListener_}

## _class_ sublime_plugin.TextChangeListener  4081
_______________________________________________________________________________

1.  Bases: [`object`][py3_object]

    A class that provides event handling about text changes made to a specific Buffer. Is separate from [`ViewEventListener`][ViewEventListener] since multiple views can share a single buffer.

2.  on_text_changed(_changes: List[[TextChange][TextChange]]_) 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_TextChangeListener_on_text_changed_}

    Called once after changes has been made to a buffer, with detailed information about what has changed.

    on_text_changed_async(changes: List[TextChange]):

    Same as [`on_text_changed`][on_text_changed] but runs in a separate thread, not blocking the application.

3.  on_revert() 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_TextChangeListener_on_revert_}

    Called when the buffer is reverted.

    A revert does not trigger text changes. If the contents of the buffer are required here use [`View.substr`][substr].

4.  on_revert_async() 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_TextChangeListener_on_revert_async_}

    Same as [`on_revert`][on_revert] but runs in a separate thread, not blocking the application.

5.  on_reload() 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_TextChangeListener_on_reload_}

    Called when the buffer is reloaded.

    A reload does not trigger text changes. If the contents of the buffer are required here use [`View.substr`][substr].

6.  on_reload_async() 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_TextChangeListener_on_reload_async_}

    Same as [`on_reload`][on_reload] but runs in a separate thread, not blocking the application.

7.  _classmethod_ is_applicable(_buffer: [Buffer][Buffer]_) 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_TextChangeListener_is_applicable_}

    Returns:

    Whether this listener should apply to the provided buffer.

8.  detach() 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_TextChangeListener_detach_}

    Remove this listener from the buffer.

    Async callbacks may still be called after this, as they are queued separately.

    Raises [`ValueError`][py3_ValueError]:

    if the listener is not attached.

9.  attach(_buffer: [Buffer][Buffer]_) 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_TextChangeListener_attach_}

    Attach this listener to a buffer.

    Raises [`ValueError`][py3_ValueError]:

    if the listener is already attached.

10.  is_attached() â†’ [bool][py3_bool] 
    [ðŸ”—](){id=sublime_plugin_TextChangeListener_is_attached_}

    Returns:

    whether the listener is receiving events from a buffer. May not be called from `__init__`.
